<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Space">Space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mathematics&amp;section=12&amp;veaction=editsource" title="Edit section: Space">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The study of space originates with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geometry" title="Geometry">geometry</a>&nbsp; in particular, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euclidean_geometry" title="Euclidean geometry">Euclidean geometry</a>, which combines space and numbers, and encompasses the well-known <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pythagorean_theorem" title="Pythagorean theorem">Pythagorean theorem</a>. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trigonometry" title="Trigonometry">Trigonometry</a> is the branch of mathematics that deals with relationships between the sides and the angles of triangles and with the trigonometric functions. The modern study of space generalizes these ideas to include higher-dimensional geometry, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-Euclidean_geometries" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-Euclidean geometries">non-Euclidean geometries</a> (which play a central role in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a>) and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topology" title="Topology">topology</a>. Quantity and space both play a role in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analytic_geometry" title="Analytic geometry">analytic geometry</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Differential_geometry" title="Differential geometry">differential geometry</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebraic_geometry" title="Algebraic geometry">algebraic geometry</a>. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convex_geometry" title="Convex geometry">Convex</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrete_geometry" title="Discrete geometry">discrete geometry</a> were developed to solve problems in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geometry_of_numbers" title="Geometry of numbers">number theory</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functional_analysis" title="Functional analysis">functional analysis</a> but now are pursued with an eye on applications in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convex_optimization" title="Convex optimization">optimization</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_geometry" title="Computational geometry">computer science</a>. Within differential geometry are the concepts of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiber_bundles" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiber bundles">fiber bundles</a> and calculus on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manifold" title="Manifold">manifolds</a>, in particular, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vector_calculus" title="Vector calculus">vector</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor_calculus" title="Tensor calculus">tensor calculus</a>. Within algebraic geometry is the description of geometric objects as solution sets of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polynomial" title="Polynomial">polynomial</a> equations, combining the concepts of quantity and space, and also the study of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topological_groups" class="mw-redirect" title="Topological groups">topological groups</a>, which combine structure and space. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lie_group" title="Lie group">Lie groups</a> are used to study space, structure, and change. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topology" title="Topology">Topology</a> in all its many ramifications may have been the greatest growth area in 20th-century mathematics; it includes <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Point-set_topology" class="mw-redirect" title="Point-set topology">point-set topology</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set-theoretic_topology" title="Set-theoretic topology">set-theoretic topology</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebraic_topology" title="Algebraic topology">algebraic topology</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Differential_topology" title="Differential topology">differential topology</a>. In particular, instances of modern-day topology are <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metrizability_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Metrizability theory">metrizability theory</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axiomatic_set_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Axiomatic set theory">axiomatic set theory</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homotopy_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Homotopy theory">homotopy theory</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morse_theory" title="Morse theory">Morse theory</a>. Topology also includes the now solved <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poincar%C3%A9_conjecture" title="Poincar conjecture">Poincar conjecture</a>, and the still unsolved areas of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hodge_conjecture" title="Hodge conjecture">Hodge conjecture</a>. Other results in geometry and topology, including the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Four_color_theorem" title="Four color theorem">four color theorem</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kepler_conjecture" title="Kepler conjecture">Kepler conjecture</a>, have been proved only with the help of computers.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Change">Change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mathematics&amp;section=13&amp;veaction=editsource" title="Edit section: Change">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Understanding and describing change is a common theme in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_science" title="Natural science">natural sciences</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calculus" title="Calculus">calculus</a> was developed as a powerful tool to investigate it. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(mathematics)" title="Function (mathematics)">Functions</a> arise here, as a central concept describing a changing quantity. The rigorous study of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_number" title="Real number">real numbers</a> and functions of a real variable is known as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_analysis" title="Real analysis">real analysis</a>, with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complex_analysis" title="Complex analysis">complex analysis</a> the equivalent field for the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complex_number" title="Complex number">complex numbers</a>. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functional_analysis" title="Functional analysis">Functional analysis</a> focuses attention on (typically infinite-dimensional) <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space#Mathematics" title="Space">spaces</a> of functions. One of many applications of functional analysis is <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum mechanics</a>. Many problems lead naturally to relationships between a quantity and its rate of change, and these are studied as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Differential_equation" title="Differential equation">differential equations</a>. Many phenomena in nature can be described by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamical_system" title="Dynamical system">dynamical systems</a>; <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaos_theory" title="Chaos theory">chaos theory</a> makes precise the ways in which many of these systems exhibit unpredictable yet still <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deterministic_system_(mathematics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Deterministic system (mathematics)">deterministic</a> behavior.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Applied_mathematics">Applied mathematics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mathematics&amp;section=14&amp;veaction=editsource" title="Edit section: Applied mathematics">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Applied_mathematics" title="Applied mathematics">Applied mathematics</a> concerns itself with mathematical methods that are typically used in science, engineering, business, and industry. Thus, "applied mathematics" is a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_science" class="mw-redirect" title="Mathematical science">mathematical science</a> with specialized knowledge. The term <i>applied mathematics</i> also describes the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Professional" title="Professional">professional</a> specialty in which mathematicians work on practical problems; as a profession focused on practical problems, <i>applied mathematics</i> focuses on the "formulation, study, and use of mathematical models" in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>, and other areas of mathematical practice.</p>
<p>In the past, practical applications have motivated the development of mathematical theories, which then became the subject of study in pure mathematics, where mathematics is developed primarily for its own sake. Thus, the activity of applied mathematics is vitally connected with research in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pure_mathematics" title="Pure mathematics">pure mathematics</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics_and_other_decision_sciences">Statistics and other decision sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mathematics&amp;section=15&amp;veaction=editsource" title="Edit section: Statistics and other decision sciences">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Applied mathematics has significant overlap with the discipline of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">statistics</a>, whose theory is formulated mathematically, especially with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probability_theory" title="Probability theory">probability theory</a>. Statisticians (working as part of a research project) "create data that makes sense" with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Random_sampling" class="mw-redirect" title="Random sampling">random sampling</a> and with randomized <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Design_of_experiments" title="Design of experiments">experiments</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics?oldformat=true#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> the design of a statistical sample or experiment specifies the analysis of the data (before the data be available). When reconsidering data from experiments and samples or when analyzing data from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Observational_study" title="Observational study">observational studies</a>, statisticians "make sense of the data" using the art of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_model" title="Statistical model">modelling</a> and the theory of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_inference" title="Statistical inference">inference</a>&nbsp; with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Model_selection" title="Model selection">model selection</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estimation_theory" title="Estimation theory">estimation</a>; the estimated models and consequential <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_method#Predictions_from_the_hypothesis" title="Scientific method">predictions</a> should be <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_hypothesis_testing" title="Statistical hypothesis testing">tested</a> on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_method#Evaluation_and_improvement" title="Scientific method">new data</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics?oldformat=true#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_theory" title="Statistical theory">Statistical theory</a> studies <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_decision_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Statistical decision theory">decision problems</a> such as minimizing the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Risk" title="Risk">risk</a> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expected_loss" title="Expected loss">expected loss</a>) of a statistical action, such as using a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_method" class="mw-redirect" title="Statistical method">procedure</a> in, for example, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parameter_estimation" class="mw-redirect" title="Parameter estimation">parameter estimation</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypothesis_testing" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypothesis testing">hypothesis testing</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selection_algorithm" title="Selection algorithm">selecting the best</a>. In these traditional areas of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_statistics" title="Mathematical statistics">mathematical statistics</a>, a statistical-decision problem is formulated by minimizing an <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Objective_function" class="mw-redirect" title="Objective function">objective function</a>, like expected loss or <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cost" title="Cost">cost</a>, under specific constraints: For example, designing a survey often involves minimizing the cost of estimating a population mean with a given level of confidence.<sup id="cite_ref-RaoOpt_54-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics?oldformat=true#cite_note-RaoOpt-54">[54]</a></sup> Because of its use of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_optimization" title="Mathematical optimization">optimization</a>, the mathematical theory of statistics shares concerns with other <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_science" class="mw-redirect" title="Decision science">decision sciences</a>, such as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operations_research" title="Operations research">operations research</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_theory" title="Control theory">control theory</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_economics" title="Mathematical economics">mathematical economics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Whittle_55-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics?oldformat=true#cite_note-Whittle-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Computational_mathematics">Computational mathematics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mathematics&amp;section=16&amp;veaction=editsource" title="Edit section: Computational mathematics">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_mathematics" title="Computational mathematics">Computational mathematics</a> proposes and studies methods for solving <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_problem" title="Mathematical problem">mathematical problems</a> that are typically too large for human numerical capacity. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_analysis" title="Numerical analysis">Numerical analysis</a> studies methods for problems in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analysis_(mathematics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Analysis (mathematics)">analysis</a> using <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functional_analysis" title="Functional analysis">functional analysis</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Approximation_theory" title="Approximation theory">approximation theory</a>; numerical analysis includes the study of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Approximation" title="Approximation">approximation</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discretization" title="Discretization">discretization</a> broadly with special concern for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rounding_error" class="mw-redirect" title="Rounding error">rounding errors</a>. Numerical analysis and, more broadly, scientific computing also study non-analytic topics of mathematical science, especially <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm" title="Algorithm">algorithmic</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_linear_algebra" title="Numerical linear algebra">matrix</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_theory" title="Graph theory">graph theory</a>. Other areas of computational mathematics include <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_algebra" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer algebra">computer algebra</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbolic_computation" title="Symbolic computation">symbolic computation</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mathematical_awards">Mathematical awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mathematics&amp;section=17&amp;veaction=editsource" title="Edit section: Mathematical awards">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Arguably the most prestigious award in mathematics is the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMonastyrsky2001_56-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics?oldformat=true#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMonastyrsky2001-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERiehm2002778.E2.80.9382_57-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics?oldformat=true#cite_note-FOOTNOTERiehm2002778.E2.80.9382-57">[57]</a></sup> established in 1936 and awarded every four years (except around World War II) to as many as four individuals. The Fields Medal is often considered a mathematical equivalent to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolf_Prize_in_Mathematics" title="Wolf Prize in Mathematics">Wolf Prize in Mathematics</a>, instituted in 1978, recognizes lifetime achievement, and another major international award, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abel_Prize" title="Abel Prize">Abel Prize</a>, was instituted in 2003. The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chern_Medal" title="Chern Medal">Chern Medal</a> was introduced in 2010 to recognize lifetime achievement. These accolades are awarded in recognition of a particular body of work, which may be innovational, or provide a solution to an outstanding problem in an established field.</p>
<p>A famous list of 23 <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_problem" title="Open problem">open problems</a>, called "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hilbert%27s_problems" title="Hilbert&#39;s problems">Hilbert's problems</a>", was compiled in 1900 by German mathematician <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Hilbert" title="David Hilbert">David Hilbert</a>. This list achieved great celebrity among mathematicians, and at least nine of the problems have now been solved. A new list of seven important problems, titled the "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Millennium_Prize_Problems" title="Millennium Prize Problems">Millennium Prize Problems</a>", was published in 2000. A solution to each of these problems carries a $1&nbsp;million reward, and only one (the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riemann_hypothesis" title="Riemann hypothesis">Riemann hypothesis</a>) is duplicated in Hilbert's problems.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mathematics&amp;section=19&amp;veaction=editsource" title="Edit section: Notes">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics?oldformat=true#cite_ref-52"><span class="cite-accessibility-label">Jump up </span>^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C.R._Rao" class="mw-redirect" title="C.R. <li id="cite_note-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics?oldformat=true#cite_ref-53"><span class="cite-accessibility-label">Jump up </span>^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Like other mathematical sciences such as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a>, statistics is an autonomous discipline rather than a branch of applied mathematics. Like research physicists and computer scientists, research statisticians are mathematical scientists. Many statisticians have a degree in mathematics, and some statisticians are also mathematicians.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-RaoOpt-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics?oldformat=true#cite_ref-RaoOpt_54-0"><span class="cite-accessibility-label">Jump up </span>^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite id="CITEREFRao1981" class="citation book"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C.R._Rao" class="mw-redirect" title="C.R. In Arthanari, T.S.; <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yadolah_Dodge" title="Yadolah Dodge">Dodge, Yadolah</a>. <i>Mathematical programming in statistics</i>. Wiley Series in Probability and Mathematical Statistics. New York: Wiley. pp.&nbsp;viiviii. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-471-08073-X" title="Special:BookSources/0-471-08073-X">0-471-08073-X</a>. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_Reviews" title="Mathematical Reviews">MR</a>&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ams.org/mathscinet-getitem?mr=607328">607328</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMathematics&amp;rft.atitle=Foreword&amp;rft.aufirst=C.R.&amp;rft.aulast=Rao&amp;rft.btitle=Mathematical+programming+in+statistics&amp;rft.date=1981&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ams.org%2Fmathscinet-getitem%3Fmr%3D607328&amp;rft.isbn=0-471-08073-X&amp;rft.pages=vii-viii&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pub=Wiley&amp;rft.series=Wiley+Series+in+Probability+and+Mathematical+Statistics&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></span></li>

<div class="refbegin" style="">
<ul>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/369194">Mathematics</a> at <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopdia Britannica">Encyclopdia Britannica</a></i></li>
<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/p00545hk">Mathematics</a> on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/In_Our_Time_(radio_series)" title="In Our Time (radio series)"><i>In Our Time</i></a> at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>. (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/iplayer/console/p00545hk/In_Our_Time_Mathematics">listen now</a>)</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://freebookcentre.net/SpecialCat/Free-Mathematics-Books-Download.html">Free Mathematics books</a> Free Mathematics books collection.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Encyclopaedia_of_Mathematics" class="mw-redirect" title="Encyclopaedia of Mathematics">Encyclopaedia of Mathematics</a> online encyclopaedia from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.encyclopediaofmath.org/">Springer</a>, Graduate-level reference work with over 8,000 entries, illuminating nearly 50,000 notions in mathematics.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://hyperphysics.phy-astr.gsu.edu/Hbase/hmat.html">HyperMath site at Georgia State University</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.freescience.info/mathematics.php">FreeScience Library</a> The mathematics section of FreeScience library</li>
<li>Rusin, Dave: <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20030130131813/http://math-atlas.org/">The Mathematical Atlas</a></i>. A guided tour through the various branches of modern mathematics. (Can also be found at <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20061006114449/http://www.math.niu.edu/~rusin/known-math/index/index.html">NIU.edu</a>.)</li>
<li>Cain, George: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.math.gatech.edu/~cain/textbooks/onlinebooks.html">Online Mathematics Textbooks</a> available free online.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tricki.org/">Tricki</a>, Wiki-style site that is intended to develop into a large store of useful mathematical problem-solving techniques.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.math.chapman.edu/~jipsen/structures/doku.php/">Mathematical Structures</a>, list information about classes of mathematical structures.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www-history.mcs.st-and.ac.uk/~history/">Mathematician Biographies</a>. The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacTutor_History_of_Mathematics_archive" title="MacTutor History of Mathematics archive">MacTutor History of Mathematics archive</a> Extensive history and quotes from all famous mathematicians.</li>
<li><i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://metamath.org/">Metamath</a></i>. A site and a language, that formalize mathematics from its foundations.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nrich.maths.org/public/index.php">Nrich</a>, a prize-winning site for students from age five from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">Cambridge University</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://garden.irmacs.sfu.ca/">Open Problem Garden</a>, a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wiki" title="Wiki">wiki</a> of open problems in mathematics</li>
<li><i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://planetmath.org/">Planet Math</a></i>. An online mathematics encyclopedia under construction, focusing on modern mathematics. Uses the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CC_BY_SA" class="mw-redirect" title="CC BY SA">Attribution-ShareAlike</a> license, allowing article exchange with Wikipedia. Uses <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TeX" title="TeX">TeX</a> markup.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060617235118/http://www-math.mit.edu/daimp/">Some mathematics applets, at MIT</a></li>
<li>Weisstein, Eric et al.: <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mathworld.wolfram.com/">Wolfram MathWorld: World of Mathematics</a></i>. An online encyclopedia of mathematics.</li>
<li>Patrick Jones' <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/user/patrickJMT">Video Tutorials</a> on Mathematics</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://en.citizendium.org/wiki/Theory_(mathematics)">Citizendium: Theory (mathematics)</a>.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_du_Sautoy" title="Marcus du Sautoy">du Sautoy, Marcus</a>, <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/podcasts/series/maths">A Brief History of Mathematics</a></i>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">BBC Radio 4</a> (2010).</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://math.stackexchange.com/">Maths.SE</a> A Q&amp;A site for mathematics</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mathoverflow.net/">MathOverflow</a> A Q&amp;A site for research-level mathematics</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://momath.org/">National Museum of Mathematics, located in New York City</a></li>
</ul>
